Nearly half of the global population already live in areas highly vulnerable to climate change. We need immediate action to help them become more resilient—or we face dire consequences. If action persists being delayed, the collapse of healthcare systems, widespread food and water shortages, and mass displacement will become our new reality.\n\nThere is simply not enough money being invested to help communities and local healthcare systems adapt to the health threats of climate change. Alarmingly, there is currently a staggering $366 billion finance gap <https://www.unep.org/resources/adaptation-gap-report-2023> when it comes to annual funding for climate adaptation, with less than 5% of climate adaptation finance being allocated to projects that protect or improve health. As stated in Source 2, the Congo Basin forests, for instance, are home to 80 million people and support life for a further 300 million rural Africans in surrounding regions [2]. The loss of these forests would have devastating consequences, including the displacement of hundreds of millions of people. Moreover, biodiversity is essential for providing ecosystem services, such as producing oxygen, serving as a carbon sink, and absorbing excess heat generated by carbon emissions, as highlighted in Source 3 [3].

Furthermore, biodiversity is critical for human well-being, as it provides numerous benefits, including food, water, and medicine. The collapse of healthcare systems, widespread food and water shortages, and mass displacement will become our new reality if we fail to address the health threats of climate change, as warned by global health leaders in Source 5 [5]. The preservation of biodiversity is, therefore, essential for maintaining the health and resilience of human populations.

In addition, biodiversity is intricately linked with climate change, and its loss can exacerbate the climate crisis. As mentioned in Source 1, the goal of protecting and restoring 30% of the Earth's land and oceans by 2030 was agreed upon by world leaders, recognizing the critical role biodiversity plays in mitigating climate change [1]. The preservation of biodiversity is, therefore, crucial for maintaining the planet's health and mitigating the worst impacts of climate change.
